dab¹
/dæb ||; dæb/verb [I,T] (dabbing;dabbed) to touch sth lightly, usually several times 轻拍，轻触（通常指数次）: He dabbed the cut with some cotton wool. 他用药棉擦拭伤口。 dab sth on/off (sth) to put sth on or to remove sth lightly 轻轻涂上或抹掉: to dab some antiseptic on a wound 在伤口上轻轻涂上一些消毒药

2 a small quantity of sth that is put on a surface （涂在平面上的）少量，一点儿（东西）: a dab of paint/perfume 一点儿漆╱香水

dabble
/ˈdæbl ||; ˈdæbḷ/verb

2 [T] to put your hands, feet, etc in water and move them around （用手、足等）溅水，戏水: We sat on the bank and dabbled our toes in the river. 我们坐在岸上，把脚趾伸进河里戏水。

*damage¹
/ˈdæmɪdʒ ||; ˈdæmɪdʒ/noun

/dæm ||; dæm/ (also damned) adj adv (slang 俚语)

2 a swear word that people use to show that they are angry （表示愤怒的诅咒语）该死的: Some damn fool has parked too close to me. 有个该死的笨蛋把车停在离我的车太近的地方。

*damp¹

damp²
/dæmp ||; dæmp/verb [T] damp sth (down)
1 to make a fire burn less strongly or stop burning 封火；灭火: He tried to damp (down) the flames. 他试图把火扑灭。
2 to make sth less strong or urgent 减弱；延缓: He tried to damp down their expectations in case they failed. 他试图给他们泼冷水，免得他们万一失败而大失所望。

dampen
/ˈdæmpən ||; ˈdæmpən/verb[T]
1 to make sth less strong or urgent 减弱；延缓: Even the awful weather did not dampen their enthusiasm for the trip. 连恶劣的天气也不能减少他们对此行的兴致。
2 to make sth a little wet 使潮湿: He dampened his hair to try to stop it sticking up. 他把头发弄湿，使它不再竖起来。

*danger
/ˈdeɪndʒə(r) ||; ˈdendʒɚ/noun
1 [U] [C] the chance that sb/sth may be hurt, killed or damaged or that sth bad may happen 危险: When he saw the men had knives, he realized his life was in danger. 他一见那几个人拿着刀子，就意识到自己有生命危险。 The men kept on running until they thought they were out of danger. 这些男子不停地跑着，直至他们认为已经脱离危险。 If things carry on as they are, there's a danger that the factory may have to close. 如果情况照此发展下去，工厂有不得不关门的危险。
2 [C] a danger (to sb/sth) a person or thing that can cause injury, pain or damage to sb 可能引起危险的人或物；威胁: Drunk drivers are a danger to everyone on the road. 喝醉的司机对马路上的每一个人都会构成威胁。

*dangerous
/ˈdeɪndʒərəs ||; ˈdendʒərəs/adj likely to cause injury or damage 危险的；有危险的: a dangerous animal/road/illness 危险的动物╱道路╱病症 Police warn that the man is highly dangerous. 警方警告说，这名男子是极其危险的。 ➔dangerously adv He was standing dangerously close to the cliff edge. 他站得很近悬崖的边缘，十分危险。

dangle
/ˈdæŋgl ||; ˈdæŋgḷ/verb [I,T] to hang freely; to hold sth so that it hangs down in this way （使）悬挂，悬垂，摇摆: She sat on the fence with her legs dangling. 她坐在栅栏上，双腿悬垂着。 The police dangled a rope from the bridge and the man grabbed it. 警察从桥上垂下一条绳子，那名男子抓住了。

*dare¹
/deə(r) ||; dɛr/verb
1 [I] (usually in negative sentences 通常用于否定句) dare (to) do sth to have enough courage to do sth 敢；敢于: Nobody dared (to) speak. 没有人敢说话。 I daren't ask her to lend me any more money. 我不敢再问她借钱了。 We were so frightened that we didn't dare (to) go into the room. 我们怕得不敢走进那个房间。
The negative is dare not (usually daren't /deənt/) or do not/does not (don't/doesn't) dare. In the past tense it is did not (didn't) dare. 否定式为dare not（通常作daren't //deənt/）或do not／does not (don't／doesn't) dare。过去时为did not (didn't) dare。
2 [T] dare sb (to do sth) to ask or tell sb to do sth in order to see if he/she has the courage to do it 激（某人）做（某事）；向（某人）挑战: Can you jump off that wall? Go on, I dare you! 你敢不敢从那墙上跳下来？跳吧，我谅你也不敢！ He dared his friend to put a mouse in the teacher's bag. 他问他的朋友敢不敢把一只老鼠放在老师的包里。
don't you dare used for telling sb very strongly not to do sth （用于郑重其事地告诉某人不要做某事）: Don't you dare tell my parents about this! 千万不要把这事告诉我父母！ how dare you used when you are angry about sth that sb has done （用于对某人的作为表示生气）你竟敢: How dare you speak to me like that! 你竟敢这样对我说话！ I dare say used when you are saying sth is probable 我敢说；我想；我以为: ‘I think you should accept the offer.’ ‘I dare say you're right.’ “我认为你应该接受这提议。”“我想你说得对。”
*dare²
/deə(r) ||; dɛr/noun [C] [usu.sing] something dangerous that sb asks you to do, to see if you have the courage to do it 挑战: ‘Why did you try to swim across the river?’ ‘ For a dare.’ “你为什么想游过这条河呢？”“受人激将。”

*dark¹
/dɑ:k ||; dɑrk/adj
1 with no light or very little light 黑暗的；阴暗的: It was a dark night, with no moon. 那天夜晚没有月光，伸手不见五指。 What time does it get dark in winter? 冬天什么时候天黑？
2 (used about a colour) not light; nearer black than white （指颜色）深色的，暗色的: dark blue 深蓝色 [OPP] light or pale 反义词为light或pale
3 (especially Brit 尤为英) (used about a person's hair, skin or eyes) brown or black; not fair （指人的头发、皮肤或眼睛）棕色的，黑色的，不是白皙的: She was small and dark with brown eyes. 她身材细小，有黑皮肤和棕色的眼睛。
4 (only before a noun 只用于名词前) hidden and frightening; mysterious 神秘的；阴险的: He seemed friendly, but there was a dark side to his character. 他看似很友好，但他的性格也有阴暗的一面。
5 (only before a noun 只用于名词前) sad; without hope 悲伤的；无望的；黯淡的: the dark days of the recession 经济衰退时的黯淡日子
*dark²
/dɑ:k ||; dɑrk/noun [sing] the dark the state of having no light 黑暗；无光: He's afraid of the dark. 他怕黑。 Why are you sitting alone in the dark ? 你为什么一个人坐在黑暗之中？ before/after dark before /after the sun goes down in the evening 日落以前或以后 (be/keep sb) in the dark (about sth) (be/keep sb) in a position of not knowing about sth （把某人）蒙在鼓里；不让（某人）知道（某事）；（对某事）毫不知情: Don't keep me in the dark. Tell me! 不要把我蒙在鼓里。告诉我吧！

dash¹
/dæʃ ||; dæʃ/noun
1 [sing] an act of going somewhere suddenly and quickly 急奔；猛冲: Suddenly the prisoner made a dash for the door. 那犯人突然间冲向门口。
2 [C] [usu.sing] a small amount of sth that you add to sth else （加入的）少量，少许: a dash of lemon juice 少许柠檬汁
3 [C] a small horizontal line (-) used in writing, especially for adding extra information 破折号（-） ☞Look at hyphen. 参看hyphen。
dash²
/dæʃ ||; dæʃ/verb
1 [I] to go somewhere suddenly and quickly 急奔；猛冲: We all dashed for shelter when it started to rain. 开始下雨时，我们全都冲向躲雨的地方。 I must dash -- I'm late. 我得飞奔过去求求我已经晚了。
2 [I,T] to hit sth with great force; to throw sth so that it hits sth else very hard 猛击；猛撞；猛掷 · She dashed her racket to the ground. 她把球拍甩到地上。
dash sb's hopes (of sth/of doing sth) to completely destroy sb's hopes of doing sth 使某人的希望破灭: The accident dashed his hopes of becoming a pianist. 那起事故使他成为钢琴家的希望顿成泡影。 dash sth off to write or draw sth very quickly 匆匆地写或画: I dashed off a note to my boss and left. 我匆匆给老板留个条就离去了。

*date¹
/deɪt ||; det/noun
1 [C] a particular day of the month or year 日期；日子: What's the date today?/What date is it today?/What's today's date? 今天是几月几日？ What's your date of birth ? 你是哪年哪月哪日出生的？ We'd better fix a date for the next meeting. 我们最好为下一次会议定个日期。
2 [sing] a particular time 某个时间: We can discuss this at a later date. 我们可以以后再讨论这个问题。 ☞Look at sell-by date. 参看sell-by date。
3 [C] an arrangement to meet sb, especially a boyfriend or girlfriend 约会（尤指男女朋友的）: Shall we make a date to have lunch together? 我们约个时间一起吃午饭好吗？ I've got a date with Roxanne on Friday night. 星期五晚上我约了罗克珊。 ☞Look at blind date. 参看blind date。
4 [C] a small, sweet, dark brown fruit that comes from a tree which grows in hot countries 枣子；海枣果 ☞picture on page C3 见C3页插图
out of date
1 not fashionable; no longer useful 过时；不再有用: out-of-date methods/machinery 过时的方法；陈旧的机器
2 no longer able to be used 已经不能再用: I must renew my passport. It's out of date. 我要换新护照，这一本已经过期啦。
to date(formal 正式) until now 到目前为止；迄今: We've had very few complaints to date. 到目前为止我们接到很少投诉。 up to date
1 completely modern 十足现代；最新: The new kitchen will be right up to date, with all the latest gadgets. 这个新厨房将会是十足现代化的，具备所有最新的小巧装置。
2 with all the latest information; having done everything that you should 有齐全和最新的资料；做了所有应该要做的事: In this report we'll bring you up to date with the latest news from the area. 在这项报道中，我们会为你提供这地区的最新消息。
*date²
/deɪt ||; det/verb
1 [T] to discover or guess how old sth is 鉴定（某物的）年代: The skeleton has been dated at about 3000 BC. 经过鉴定，这是大约公元前3000年的骸骨。
2 [T] to write the day's date on sth 注明日期；写上日期: The letter is dated 24 March, 2000. 这封信上的日期是2000年3月24日。
3 [I,T] to seem, or to make sb/sth seem, unfashionable （使）看来过时，显得不流行: We chose a simple style so that it wouldn't date as quickly. 为了不会很快便显得过时，我们选了一种简单的款式。
date back to...; date from... to have existed since... 自（某时代）存在至今；可上溯自…: The house dates back to the seventeenth century. 这房子是十七世纪建的。 photographs dating from before the war 战前留下来的照片

/dɔ:n ||; dɔn/noun
1 [U] [C] the early morning, when light first appears in the sky 破晓；黎明: before/at dawn 黎明之前；黎明之时: Dawn was breaking (= it was starting to get light) as I set off to work. 我出发上班的时候，天刚开始亮。

dawn²
/dɔ:n ||; dɔn/verb[I]
1 (formal 正式) to begin to grow light, after the night 破晓；（天）初亮: The day dawned bright and cold. 天初亮时，晴朗而寒冷。 (figurative 比喻) A new era of peace is dawning. 一个和平的新纪元正初露曙光。
2 dawn (on sb) to become clear (to sb) 变得明白；领悟: Suddenly it dawned on her. ‘Of course!’ she said. ‘You're Mike's brother!’ 她忽然明白过来。“当然啦！”她说，“你是迈克的弟弟！”

*day
/deɪ ||; de/noun
1 [C] a period of 24 hours. Seven days make up a week 一日；一天: ‘What day is it today?’ ‘Tuesday.’ “今天是星期几？”“星期二。” We went to Italy for ten days. 我们去了意大利十天。 We're meeting again the day after tomorrow/in two days' time. 我们后天又要见面。 The next/following day I saw Mark again. 次日我又见过马克。 I'd already spoken to him the day before/the previous day. 我前一天已经跟他说过话。 I have to take these pills twice a day. 这些药片我一天得服两次。 I work six days a week. Sunday's my day off (= when I do not work). 我每周工作六天。星期日我不上班。
2 [C,U] the time when the sky is light; not night 日间；白天；白昼: The days were warm but the nights were freezing. 白天暖和，但晚上冷得很。 It's been raining all day (long). 下了一整天雨。 Owls sleep by day (= during the day) and hunt at night. 猫头鹰白天睡觉，夜间猎食。
3 [C] the hours of the day when you work 工作时间；上班时间: She's expected to work a seven-hour day. 她每天要上七个小时班。
4 [C] (also days) a particular period of time in the past （过去的某一）时代，时期: in Shakespeare's day 在莎士比亚时代 There weren't so many cars in those days. 那个时代没有这么多汽车。
at the end of the day→END¹ break of day→BREAK² call it a day→CALL¹ day by day every day; as time passes 一天天: Day by day, she was getting a little bit stronger. 她一天天强壮起来。 day in, day out every day, without any change 日复一日；不间断: He sits at his desk working, day in, day out. 他日复一日伏案工作。 day-to-day happening as a normal part of each day; usual 每天的；日常的 from day to day;from one day to the next within a short period of time 在短时间之内: Things change so quickly that we never know what will happen from one day to the next. 事物变化得这么快，我们根本无法知道明天会发生什么事。 have a field day→FIELD DAY it's early days (yet)→EARLY make sb's day(informal 非正式) to make sb very happy 使某人十分高兴 one day;some day at some time in the future 将来有一天；他日: Some day we'll go back and see all our old friends. 有朝一日我们会回去看望所有的老朋友。 the other day a few days ago; recently 前几天；最近: I bumped into him in town the other day. 前几天我在城里碰见他。 the present day→PRESENT¹ these days in the present age; nowadays 现在；目前；如今

*dead¹
/ded ||; dɛd/adj
1 no longer alive 死的；已死的: My father's dead. He died two years ago. 我的父亲已经去世。他是两年前死的。 Police found a dead body under the bridge. 警方在桥底下发现一具尸体。 The man was shot dead by a masked gunman. 那男子被一个蒙面枪手开枪打死。 dead leaves 枯叶 ☞noun death, verb die 名词为death，动词为die
2 no longer used; finished 已不用的；已完结的: Latin is a dead language. 拉丁文是死的语言。 [OPP] living 反义词为living
3 (not before a noun 不用于名词前) (used about a part of the body) no longer able to feel anything （指身体某部份）麻木，无感觉: Oh no, my foot's gone dead. I was sitting on it for too long. 啊呀，我的一只脚麻木了。我垫着它坐了太久。
4 (not before a noun 不用于名词前) (used about a piece of equipment) no longer working （指设备）失灵: I picked up the telephone but the line was dead. 我拿起电话，但线路坏了。 This battery's dead. 这节电池没有电了。
5 without movement, activity or interest 静止的；无活动的；无趣味的: This town is completely dead after 11 o'clock at night. 这市镇晚上过了11点钟一片死寂。
6 (only before a noun 只用于名词前) complete or exact 完全的；绝对的: a dead silence/calm 一片死寂；完全的平静 The arrow hit the dead centre of the target. 那箭不偏不倚，正中靶心。

*deal¹
/di:l ||; dil/verb (past tense past participle dealt /delt ||; dɛlt/)
1 [I,T] deal (sth) (out);deal (sth) (to sb) to give cards to players in a game of cards （纸牌游戏中）发牌: Start by dealing seven cards to each player. 先给每人发七张牌。
2 [I] deal (in sth);deal (with sb) to do business, especially buying and selling goods 做生意（尤指买卖货物）: He deals in second-hand cars. 他经营二手车。 Our firm deals with customers all over the world. 我们的公司跟世界各地的顾客做生意。

deal sb/sth a blow;deal a blow to sb/sth
1 to hit sb/sth 打击: He was dealt a nasty blow to the head in the accident. 他在那起事故中头上重重地挨了一击。
2 to give sb a shock, etc 使某人震惊等: This news dealt a terrible blow to my father. 这消息给了我父亲沉重的打击。
deal sth out to give sth to a number of people 分配；分发: The profits will be dealt out among us. 利润将由我们大家来分。 deal with sb to treat sb in a particular way; to handle sb 对待；对付: He's a difficult man. Nobody quite knows how to deal with him. 他是个不易相处的人。谁也不知道怎样与他打交道。 deal with sth
1 to take suitable action in a particular situation in order to solve a problem, complete a task, etc; to handle sth 应付，处理（问题、事务等）: My secretary will deal with my correspondence while I'm away. 我外出的时候，我的秘书会处理我的书信。
2 to have sth as its subject 以某物作为内容: This chapter deals with letter writing. 这一章是有关书信写作的。
*deal²
/di:l ||; dil/noun[C]
1 an agreement or arrangement, especially in business 交易，协议（尤指商业的）: We're hoping to do a deal with an Italian company. 我们希望跟一家意大利公司达成协议。 Let's make a deal not to criticize each other's work. 我们立个约定，不批评对方的工作。 ‘I'll help you with your essay if you'll fix my bike.’ ‘OK, it's a deal!’ “要是你帮我修自行车，我就帮你写文章。”“好吧，一言为定。”
2 the way that sb is treated 待遇；对待的方式: With high fares and unreliable services, rail users are getting a raw deal. 收费高，服务又不可靠，使用铁路的人受到了不公平的待遇。 The new law aims to give pensioners a fair deal. 这项新法律旨在使领退休金的人享受公平待遇。
3 the action of giving cards to players in a card game （纸牌游戏中的）发牌

*death

1 [C,U] the end of sb/sth's life; dying 死亡；逝世: There were two deaths and many other people were injured in the accident. 这起事故中有两人死亡，很多人受伤。 The police do not know the cause of death. 警方不知道死因。 There was no food and people were starving to death. 那里断粮了，人们快要饿死了。 ☞adjective dead, verb die 形容词为dead，动词为die
2 [U] the end (of sth) 结束；终结: the death of fascism 法西斯主义的灭亡
catch your death→CATCH¹ a matter of life and/or death→MATTER¹ put sb to death (usually passive 通常用于被动语态) (formal 正式) to kill sb as a punishment, in past times （古时）处死，杀死 sick to death of sb/sth→SICK¹ sudden death→SUDDEN

deathly
/ˈdeθli ||; ˈdɛθlɪ/adj adv like death 如死一般: There was a deathly silence. 这时一片死寂。

ˈdeath penalty
noun [sing] the legal punishment of being killed for a crime 死刑 ☞Look at capital punishment. 参看capital punishment。

ˌdeath ˈrow
noun [U] (especially in the US 尤用于美国) the cells in a prison for prisoners who are waiting to be killed as punishment for a serious crime （监狱的）死囚区: prisoners on death row 死囚区的犯人

ˈdeath toll
noun [C] the number of people killed in a disaster, war, accident, etc （灾难、战争、事故等的）死亡人数

ˈdeath trap
noun [C] a building, road, vehicle, etc that is dangerous and could cause sb's death 死亡陷阱（危及人命的建筑、道路、车辆等）

debase
/dɪˈbeɪs ||; dɪˈbes/verb [T] (usually passive 通常用于被动语态) (formal 正式) to reduce the quality or value of sth 降低（质量或价值）

debatable
/dɪˈbeɪtəbl ||; dɪˈbetəbḷ/adj not certain; that you could argue about 不肯定的；可争辩的: It's debatable whether people have a better lifestyle these days. 现在人的生活方式是否比过去要好，这是个可争辩的问题。

/dɪˈbeɪt ||; dɪˈbet/noun

2 [U] general discussion about sth expressing different opinions 讨论；辩论: There's been a lot of debate about the cause of acid rain. 有很多人议论过酸雨的成因。

/dɪˈbeɪt ||; dɪˈbet/verb

2 [T] to think about or discuss sth before deciding what to do 考虑；讨论: They debated whether to go or not. 他们讨论到底去还是不去。

debauched

*debt
/det ||; dɛt/noun
1 [C] an amount of money that you owe to sb 债；欠款；债务: She borrowed a lot of money and she's still paying off the debt. 她借了很多钱，到现在还没有还清所有欠款。
2 [U] the state of owing money 负债: After he lost his job, he got into debt. 他失业以后便开始负债。
3 [C] [usu.sing] (formal 正式) something that you owe sb, for example because he/she has helped or been kind to you 人情债；恩惠: In his speech he acknowledged his debt to his family and friends for their support. 在演说中，他对家人和朋友们给予他的支持表示深切谢意。
be in/out of debt to owe/not owe money 欠或不欠债 be in sb's debt(formal 正式) to feel grateful to sb for sth that he/she has done for you 感激某人给予恩惠

deceptive

*decide
/dɪˈsaɪd ||; dɪˈsaɪd/verb
1 [I,T] decide (to do sth);decide against (doing) sth;decide about/on sth;decide that... to think about two or more possibilities and choose one of them 选定；决定: There are so many to choose from -- I can't decide! 有这么多选择，我拿不定主意！ We've decided not to invite Isabel. 我们决定不邀请伊萨贝尔。 She decided against borrowing the money. 她决定不借这笔钱。 They decided on a name for the baby. 他们为婴孩选定了名字。 He decided that it was too late to go. 太晚了，他决定不去了。 The date hasn't been decided yet. 日期还没有定好。
2 [T] to influence sth so that it produces a particular result 起决定作用；决定（结果）: Your votes will decide the winner. 你们投的票将决定谁是优胜者。
3 [T] to cause sb to make a decision 使（某人）作决定: What finally decided you to leave? 最终是什么使你决定离开？ ☞noun decision, adjective decisive 名词为decision，形容词为decisive

decided
/dɪˈsaɪdɪd ||; dɪˈsaɪdɪd/adj clear; definite 清楚的；明确的: There has been a decided improvement in his work. 他在工作上已有明显的改善。 ☞Compare undecided. 与undecided比较。 ➔decidedly adv

decimal²
/ˈdesɪml ||; ˈdɛsəmḷ/ (also ˌdecimal ˈfraction) noun [C] (mathematics数学) a FRACTION (= a number less than one) that is shown as a decimal point followed by the number of TENTHS, HUNDREDTHS, etc 小数；十进小数: Three quarters expressed as a decimal is 0.75. 四分之三以小数表示就是0.75。 ☞Compare vulgar fraction. 与vulgar fraction比较。

*decision
/dɪˈsɪʒn ||; dɪˈsɪʒən/noun
1 [C,U] a decision (to do sth);a decision on/about sth;a decision that... a choice or judgement that you make after thinking about various possibilities 决定: Have you made a decision yet? 你作出决定没有？ I realize now that I made the wrong decision. 我现在发觉我作出了错误的决定。 There were good reasons for his decision to leave. 他决定离开是有充分理由的。 I took the decision that I believed to be right. 我作出了我认为是正确的决定。

3 [I,T] (grammar语法) if a noun, an adjective or a pronoun declines, it has different forms according to whether it is the subject or the object of a verb, whether it is in the SINGULAR or plural, etc. When you decline a noun, etc, you list these forms. 使（名词、形容词或代词）发生词尾变化

*decrease¹

*decrease²
/ˈdi:kri:s ||; ˈdikris/noun [C,U] (a) decrease (in sth) the process of becoming or making sth smaller or less; the amount that sth is reduced by 减少；降低；减少之量 [C] a 10% decrease in sales 销售额下降一成

dedicate
/ˈdedɪkeɪt ||; ˈdɛdəˌket/verb[T]
1 dedicate sth to sth to give all your energy, time, efforts, etc to sth 奉献（精力、时间、努力等）: He dedicated his life to helping the poor. 他毕生致力于帮助穷人。
2 dedicate sth to sb to say that sth is specially for sb 题献辞: He dedicated the book he had written to his brother. 他把自己写的那本书题献给了兄长。

/ˈdedɪkeɪtɪd ||; ˈdɛdəˌketɪd/adj giving a lot of your energy, time, efforts, etc to sth that you believe to be important 一心一意的；献身的: dedicated nurses and doctors 献身于工作的护士和医生

/ˌdedɪˈkeɪʃn ||; ˌdɛdəˈkeʃən/noun

deduce
/dɪˈdju:s ||; dɪˈdjus/verb [T] to form an opinion using the facts that you already know 推想；推断；演绎: From his name I deduced that he was Polish. 我从他的名字推想出他是波兰人。 ☞noun deduction 名词为deduction

deduct
/dɪˈdʌkt ||; dɪˈdʌkt/verb [T] deduct sth (from sth) to take sth such as money or points away from a total amount 减除；扣除: Marks will be deducted for untidy work. 功课不整洁要扣分。

deduction
/dɪˈdʌkʃn ||; dɪˈdʌkʃən/noun[C,U]
1 something that you work out from facts that you already know; the ability to think in this way 推断出的结论；演绎法: It was a brilliant piece of deduction by the detective. 那侦探真聪明，能够推断出这个结论。 ☞verb deduce 动词为deduce ☞Compare induction (2). 与induction(2)比较。
2 deduction (from sth) taking away an amount or number from a total; the amount or number taken away from the total 扣除；扣除额: What is your total income after deductions? (= when tax, insurance, etc are taken away) 扣除税款、保险金等各项费用后，你的总收入是多少？ ☞verb deduct 动词为deduct

/dɪˈdʌktɪv ||; dɪˈdʌktɪv/adj using knowledge about things that are generally true in order to think about and understand particular situations or problems 推论的；演绎的 ☞Compare inductive. 与inductive比较。

*deep¹
/di:p ||; dip/adj
1 going a long way down from the surface 深的（由上至下）: to dig a deep hole 掘一个深坑 That's a deep cut. 伤口很深。 a coat with deep pockets 有很深衣袋的大衣 ☞noun depth 名词为depth ☞picture at shallow 见shallow插图
2 going a long way from front to back 深的（由前至后）: deep shelves 纵深很深的架子
3 measuring a particular amount from top to bottom or from front to back 深度为…的: The water is only a metre deep at this end of the pool. 泳池这端的水只有一米深。 shelves 40 centimetres deep 40厘米深的架子
4 (used about sounds) low （指声音）低沉的: a deep voice 低沉的声音
5 (used about colours) dark; strong （指颜色）深的，浓的: a deep red 深红色
6 (used about an emotion) strongly felt （指感情）强烈感到的: He felt a very deep love for the child. 他深深地爱着这孩子。
7 (used about sleep) not easy to wake from （指睡眠）不易醒来的，熟的: I was in a deep sleep and didn't hear the phone ringing for ages. 我睡得很熟，电话铃响了半天都没有听见。
8 dealing with difficult subjects or details; thorough 深入的；透彻的: His books show a deep understanding of human nature. 他的著作流露出对人性深入的了解。 the deep noun [U]: in the deep of the night (= in the middle of the night) 在深夜 the deep (= a literary way of referring to the sea) 大海（文学用语） ➔deeply adv a deeply unhappy person 极不快乐的人 to breathe deeply 深深地呼吸
deep in thought/conversation thinking very hard or giving sb/sth your full attention 沉思；专心交谈 take a deep breath to breathe in a lot of air, especially in preparation for doing something difficult 深深地吸一口气（尤指准备做难事时）: He took a deep breath then walked on stage. 他深深地吸了口气，然后走上舞台。
*deep²
/di:p ||; dip/adv a long way down or inside sth 深深地: He gazed deep into her eyes. 他直视着她的眼睛。 He dug his hands deep into his pockets. 他把两手插到衣袋深处。 deep down in what you really think or feel 在内心深处；在心底；骨子里: I tried to appear optimistic but deep down I knew there was no hope. 我尽量表现得乐观，但在心底里知道是没有希望的。 dig deep→DIG¹

deer
/dɪə(r) ||; dɪr/noun [C] (plural deer) a large wild grass-eating animal. The male has large horns shaped like branches (antlers). 鹿 A male deer is called a buck or, especially if it has fully-grown antlers, a stag. The female is a doe and a young deer a fawn. Venison is the meat from deer. 雄鹿叫buck或stag﹔stag尤指鹿角完全成熟的雄鹿。雌鹿叫doe﹐幼鹿叫fawn。鹿肉是venison。

default¹
/dɪˈfɔ:lt ||; dɪˈfɔlt/noun [sing] (computing计算机技术) a course of action taken by a computer when it is not given any other instruction 缺省设定，缺设（计算机没有接收到其他任何指令时自行设定的选择） by default because nothing happened, not because of successful effort 因对方弃权或缺席（而获胜等）: They won by default, because the other team didn't turn up. 他们因另一队没有到场而以对方弃权获胜。

*defeat¹
/dɪˈfi:t ||; dɪˈfit/verb[T]
1 to win a game, a fight, a vote, etc against sb; to beat sb 击败；战胜；胜过: The army defeated the rebels after three days of fighting. 军队经过三天的战斗终于击败了叛乱分子。 In the last match France defeated Wales. 在最后一场比赛中法国击败了威尔士。
2 to be too difficult for sb to do or understand （因太难而）使（某人）做不到或不明白: I've tried to work out what's wrong with the car but it defeats me. 我想要找出车子有什么问题，但始终不得要领。
3 to prevent sth from succeeding 挫败；阻挠: The local residents are determined to defeat the council's building plans. 当地居民决心挫败议会的兴建计划。
defeat²
/dɪˈfi:t ||; dɪˈfit/noun
1 [C] an occasion when sb fails to win or be successful against sb else 输掉；败北；失利: This season they have had two victories and three defeats. 本赛季他们已两胜三输。
2 [U] the act of losing or not being successful 失败；输: She refused to admit defeat and kept on trying. 她拒绝承认失败，并且继续尝试。

/dɪˈfi:tɪzəm ||; dɪˈfitɪzəm/noun [U] the attitude of expecting sth to end in failure 失败主义（预料事情最终都会失败）

defeatist

*defence
/dɪˈfens ||; dɪˈfɛns/ (US 美 defense) noun
1 [U] something that you do or say to protect sb/sth from attack, bad treatment, criticism, etc 防恒；保恒；辩护: Would you fight in defence of your country? 你愿不愿为保恒国家而战？ When her brother was criticized she leapt to his defence. 当她的弟弟受到批评的时候，她挺身为他辩解。 I must say in her defencethat I have always found her very reliable. 我必须为她说句好话，我一向认为她十分可靠。 ☞Look at self-defence. 参看self-defence。
2 [C] a defence (against sth) something that protects sb/sth from sth, or that is used to fight against attack 防御物；抵抗力: the body's defences against disease 人体对疾病的抵抗力
3 [U] the military equipment, forces, etc for protecting a country 国防（为保恒国家而设的军备、军队等）: Spending on defence needs to be reduced. 国防开支有必要削减。
4 [C] (in law) an argument in support of the accused person in a court of law （法律）被告的答辩，辩护，辩词: His defence was that he was only carrying out orders. 他辩称自己不过是执行命令而已。
5 the defence [sing] [with.sop] (in law) the lawyer or lawyers who are acting for the accused person in a court of law （法律）辩方律师，辩护律师，被告律师: The defence claims/claim that many of the witnesses were lying. 被告律师声称，多位证人都在说谎。 ☞Look at the prosecution. 参看the prosecution。
6 usuallythe defence [sing] [U] (in sport) action to prevent the other team scoring; the players who try to do this （体育）防守；防守队员；后恒: She plays in defence. 她打防守。

*defend
/dɪˈfend ||; dɪˈfɛnd/verb
1 [T] defend sb/sth/yourself (against/from sb/sth) to protect sb/sth from harm or danger 保护；保恒: Would you be able to defend yourself if someone attacked you in the street? 如果你在街上遇袭，你有没有能力自恒？
2 [T] defend sb/sth/yourself (against/from sb/sth) to say or write sth to support sb/sth that has been criticized 为…辩护；为…辩解: The minister went on television to defend the government's policy. 部长上电视为政府的政策辩护。
3 [T] (in law) to speak for sb who is accused of a crime in a court of law （法律）为（被告）辩护
4 [I,T] (in sport) to try to stop the other team or player scoring （体育）防守: They defended well and managed to hold onto their lead. 他们防守很好，因此得以保持领先的优势。
5 [T] to take part in a competition that you won before and try to win it again 恒冕: She successfully defended her title. 她恒冕成功了。 He is the defending champion. 他是恒冕冠军。

defensive¹

/ˈdefərəns ||; ˈdɛfərəns/noun [U] polite behaviour that you show towards sb/sth, usually because you respect him/her 尊重；尊敬 in deference to sb/sth because you respect and do not wish to upset sb 出于尊重；为了尊重某人、不想令其不悦: In deference to her father's wishes, she didn't mention the subject again. 为了尊重父亲的意愿，她没有再提起那话题。

deformed
/dɪˈfɔ:md ||; dɪˈfɔrmd/adj having a shape that is not normal because it has grown wrongly 畸形的；变形的

deformity
/dɪˈfɔ:məti ||; dɪˈfɔrmətɪ/noun (plural deformities) [C,U] the condition of having a part of the body that is an unusual shape because of disease, injury, etc （身体）畸形，变形: The drug caused women to give birth to babies with severe deformities. 这种药物使妇女产下严重畸形的婴儿。

defraud
/dɪˈfrɔ:d ||; dɪˈfrɔd/verb [T] defraud sb (of sth) to get sth from sb in a dishonest way 骗取；诈取: He defrauded the company of millions. 他骗取了公司数百万元。

defrost
/ˌdi:ˈfrɒst; US ˌdi:ˈfrɔ:st ||; diˈfrɔst/verb
1 [T] to remove the ice from sth 除去（某物的）冰霜；给…除霜: to defrost a fridge 给冰箱除霜
2 [I,T] (used about frozen food) to return to a normal temperature; to make food do this （指冷藏食品）（使）解冻 · Defrost the chicken thoroughly before cooking. 把鸡完全解冻以后再煮。 ☞Look at de-ice. 参看de-ice。

deft
/deft ||; dɛft/adj (used especially about movements) skilful and quick （尤指动作）灵巧的，敏捷的 ➔deftly adv

defunct
/dɪˈfʌŋkt ||; dɪˈfʌŋkt/adj no longer existing or in use 不再存在的；不再使用的；过时的

defuse
/ˌdi:ˈfju:z ||; diˈfjuz/verb[T]
1 to remove part of a bomb so that it cannot explode 拆除（炸弹的）信管: Army experts defused the bomb safely. 军队专家安妥地拆去了那炸弹的引信。
2 to make a situation calmer or less dangerous 缓和；平息: She defused the tension by changing the subject. 她改变话题，缓和了紧张的气氛。

defy
/dɪˈfaɪ ||; dɪˈfaɪ/verb [T] (past participle defying third person singular present defies;past tense past participle defied)
1 to refuse to obey sb/sth 反抗；蔑视；违抗: She defied her parents and continued seeing him. 她不听从父母的话，继续和他来往。 ☞adjective defiant, noun defiance 形容词为defiant，名词为defiance
2 defy sb to do sth to ask sb to do sth that you believe to be impossible 激（某人）做（你认为不可能的事）: I defy you to prove me wrong. 我敢说你不能证明我是错的。
3 to make sth impossible or very difficult 使没有可能；使很困难: It's such a beautiful place that it defies description. 那地方美丽极了，简直是笔墨也难以形容。

degenerate¹
/dɪˈdʒenəreɪt ||; dɪˈdʒɛnəˌret/verb [I] to become worse, lower in quality, etc 退步；堕落；恶化: The calm discussion degenerated into a nasty argument. 心平气和的讨论演变为一场不愉快的争论。 ➔degeneration /dɪˌdʒenəˈreɪʃn ||; dɪˌdʒɛnəˈreʃən/ noun [U]
degenerate²
/dɪˈdʒenərət ||; dɪˈdʒɛnərət/adj having moral standards that have fallen to a very low level 道德败坏的；堕落的

degenerative
/dɪˈdʒenərətɪv ||; dɪˈdʒɛnərətɪv/adj (technical 术语) (of an illness) getting worse or likely to get worse as time passes ﹙疾病﹚变性的: degenerative diseases such as Alzheimer's 诸如阿尔茨海默氏病之类的变性病

degradation
/ˌdegrəˈdeɪʃn ||; ˌdɛgrəˈdeʃən/noun [U]:
1 the action of making sb be less respected; the state of being less respected 降低身分；丢脸: the degradation of being in prison 坐牢这种丢脸的事
2 causing the condition of sth to become worse 退化；恶化: environmental degradation 环境恶化

*degree
/dɪˈgri: ||; dɪˈgri/noun
1 [C] a measurement of temperature 度（温度的量度单位）: Water boils at 100 degrees Celsius (100° C). 水在摄氏100度沸腾。 three degrees below zero/minus three degrees (-3°) 零下三度；负三度
2 [C] a measurement of angles 度（角的量度单位）: a forty-five degree (45°) angle 45度角 An angle of 90 degrees is called a right angle. 90度角称为直角。
3 [C,U] (used about feelings or qualities) a certain amount or level （指感觉或质量）程度，水平: There is always a degree of risk involved in mountaineering. 登山总有某种程度的危险。 I sympathize with her to some degree. 我在某种程度上同情她。
4 [C] an official document gained by successfully completing a course at university or college 学位: She's got a degree in Philosophy. 她取得哲学学位。 to do aChemistry degree 攻读化学学位
In Britain degree is the usual word for the qualification you get when you complete and pass a university course. You can study for a diploma at other types of college. The courses may be shorter and more practical than degree courses. The best result you can get in a British university degree is a first, followed by a two-one, a two-two, a third, a pass, and a fail. 在英国，学位(degree)通常指完成并通过一个大学课程而取得的资格。文凭(diploma)是其他种类的院校颁授的。这些文凭课程比学位课程为期较短，同时亦多以实用为主。英国大学学位课程的最佳成绩叫做“一等”(first)，其次是“二等一级”(two-one)、“二等二级”(two-two)、“三等”(third)、“及格”(pass)及“不及格”(fail)。

dehydrate
/ˌdi:ˈhaɪdreɪt ||; diˈhaɪdret/verb
1 [T] (usually passive 通常用于被动语态) to remove all the water from sth 使脱水: Dehydrated vegetables can be stored for months. 脱水蔬菜可以保存好几个月。
2 [I,T] to lose too much water from your body （身体）脱水，失水: If you run for a long time in the heat, you start to dehydrate. 在炎热的天气里长时间跑步，你会开始脱水。 ➔dehydration /ˌdi:haɪˈdreɪʃn ||; ˌdihaɪˈdreʃən/ noun [U]: Several of the runners were suffering from severe dehydration. 有几名赛跑运动员患了严重的脱水症。

*delay¹

*deliberate¹

2 done slowly and carefully, without hurrying 从容而谨慎的: She spoke in a calm, deliberate voice. 她以平静而从容的声调说话。

delicacy

3 [C] a type of food that is considered particularly good 珍馐；佳肴；名菜: Try this dish, it's a local delicacy. 试试这个，这是本地的名菜。

*delicate
/ˈdelɪkət ||; ˈdɛləkət/adj
1 easy to damage or break 易坏的；易碎的: delicate skin 细嫩的皮肤 the delicate mechanisms of a watch 手表的精密机械结构
2 frequently ill or hurt 体弱的；易生病的: He was a delicate child and often in hospital. 他是个体弱的孩子，常常要住医院。
3 (used about colours, flavours, etc) light and pleasant; not strong （指颜色、味道等）柔和的，怡人的，淡的: a delicate shade of pale blue 柔和的淡蓝色
4 needing skilful treatment and care 需要技巧和小心处理的: Repairing this is going to be a very delicate operation. 修理这个是一件极需要技巧的工作。 ➔delicately adv She stepped delicately over the broken glass. 她小心地跨过那些碎玻璃。

*demand¹
/dɪˈmɑ:nd; US dɪˈmænd ||; dɪˈmænd/noun
1 [C] a demand (for sth/that...) a strong request or order that must be obeyed 要求；命令: a demand for changes in the law 要求修改法律 I was amazed by their demand that I should leave immediately. 他们要求我立即离开，这使我大吃一惊。
2 demands [pl] something that sb makes you do, especially sth that is difficult or tiring 要求做的事（尤指难事或累事）: Running a marathon makes huge demandson the body. 马拉松比赛极耗体力。
3 [U] [sing] demand (for sth/sb) the desire or need for sth among a group of people （一群人的）需要，需求: We no longer sell that product because there is no demand for it. 我们不再出售那种产品，因为没有人买。
in demand wanted by a lot of people 有需求；受欢迎: I'm in demand this weekend -- I've had three invitations! 这个周末我很受欢迎──已经收到三封请帖！ on demand whenever you ask for it 一经要求: This treatment is available from your doctor on demand. 只要你提出要求，医生就会为你进行这种治疗。
*demand²
/dɪˈmɑ:nd; US dɪˈmænd ||; dɪˈmænd/verb[T]
1 demand to do sth/that...;demand sth to ask for sth in an extremely firm or aggressive way 要求: I walked into the office and demanded to see the manager. 我走进办公室，要求见经理。 She demanded that I pay her immediately. 她要求我立即付钱给她。 Your behaviour was disgraceful and I demand an apology. 你的行为很可耻，我要求你道歉。
2 to need sth 需要: a sport that demands skill as well as strength 一项需要技能及体力的运动

demanding
/dɪˈmɑ:ndɪŋ; US dɪˈmændɪŋ ||; dɪˈmændɪŋ/adj
1 (used about a job, task, etc) needing a lot of effort, care, skill, etc （指工作、任务等）费力的，需要十分仔细、高度技巧的: It will be a demanding schedule -- I have to go to six cities in six days. 旅行日程安排得非常紧凑──我要在六天内去六个城市。
2 (used about a person) always wanting attention or expecting very high standards of people （指人）时刻需要照顾的，要求高的，苛求的: Young children are very demanding. 幼儿需要悉心照顾。 a demanding boss 要求严格的上司

demo
/ˈdeməʊ ||; ˈdɛmo/noun [C] (plural demos)=DEMONSTRATION(2)(3)

demo-
prefix (in nouns, adjectives and verbs 用于构成名词、形容词及动词) connected with people or population 与人或人口有关: democracy 民主

*democracy
/dɪˈmɒkrəsi ||; dəˈmɑkrəsɪ/noun (plural democracies)
1 [U] a system in which the government of a country is elected by the people 民主政治；民主政体；民主制度
2 [C] a country that has this system 民主国家
3 [U] the right of everyone in an organization, etc to be treated equally and to vote on matters that affect them 民主；民主精神；民主管理: There is a need for more democracy in the company. 这家公司需要多一点民主。

democrat
/ˈdeməkræt ||; ˈdɛməˌkræt/noun[C]
1 a person who believes in and supports democracy 民主主义者；民主人士
2 Democrat a member or supporter of the Democratic Party of the US 美国民主党的党员或支持者 ☞Look at Republican. 参看Republican。

*democratic
/ˌdeməˈkrætɪk ||; ˌdɛməˈkrætɪk/adj
1 based on the system of democracy 民主主义的；民主政制的: democratic elections 民主选举 a democratic government 民主政府
2 having or supporting equal rights for all people 民主的；民主作风的；民主精神的: a democratic decision(= made by all the people involved) 民主的决定 [OPP] undemocratic 反义词为undemocratic ➔democratically /-kli ||; -klɪ/ adv a democratically elected government 以民主方式选出的政府

/dɪˈmɒgrəfi ||; dɪˈmɑgrəfɪ/noun [U] the changing number of births, deaths, diseases, etc in a community over a period of time; the scientific study of these changes 人口变化；人口统计学: the social demography of Africa 非洲的社会人口变化 ➔demographic /ˌdeməˈgræfɪk ||; ˌdɛməˈgræfɪk/ adj demographic changes/trends/factors 人口变化；人口变化趋势；人口变化因素

/dɪˈmɒlɪʃ ||; dɪˈmɑlɪʃ/verb [T] to destroy sth, for example a building 拆毁，拆除（建筑物等）: The old shops were demolished and a supermarket was built in their place. 那些旧商店拆除后，原地盖起了一家超级市场。 (figurative 比喻) She demolished his argument in one sentence. 她用一句话便推翻了他的论点。 ➔demolition /ˌdeməˈlɪʃn ||; ˌdɛməˈlɪʃən/ noun [C,U]

*demonstrate
/ˈdemənstreɪt ||; ˈdɛmənˌstret/verb
1 [T] demonstrate sth (to sb) to show sth clearly by giving proof 表明；论证；证明: Using this chart, I'd like to demonstrate to you what has happened to our sales. 我想用这张图表来向你说明我们的销售情况。
2 [I,T] demonstrate sth (to sb) to show and explain to sb how to do sth or how sth works 示范 · The crew demonstrated the use of lifejackets just after take-off. 乘务员在飞机起飞后即示范救生衣的使用方法。 I'm not sure what you mean -- could you demonstrate? 我不大明白你的意思─你可否示范一下？
3 [I] demonstrate (against/for sb/sth) to take part in a public protest for or against sb/sth 示威；参加示威活动: Enormous crowds have been demonstrating against the government. 一直有大批群众举行反政府示威。

*demonstration
/ˌdemənˈstreɪʃn ||; ˌdɛmənˈstreʃən/noun
1 [C,U] something that shows clearly that sth exists or is true 论证；证明: This accident is a clear demonstration of the system's faults. 这宗意外清楚地证明了这系统的弊端。
2 [C,U] an act of showing or explaining to sb how to do sth or how sth works 示范: The salesman gave me a demonstration of what the computer could do. 售货员向我示范那部计算机的功能。
3 [C] a demonstration (against/for sb/sth) a public protest for or against sb/sth 示威: demonstrations against a new law 反对新法律的示威游行

demonstrative
/dɪˈmɒnstrətɪv ||; dɪˈmɑnstrətɪv/adj

2 (grammar语法) used to identify the person or thing that is being referred to 指示的: 'This' and 'that' are demonstrative pronouns. this及that是指示代词。

*depend
/dɪˈpend ||; dɪˈpɛnd/verb that depends; it (all) depends (used alone or at the beginning of a sentence 单独使用或用于句首) used to say that you are not certain of sth until other things have been considered 那得看情况而定: ‘Can you lend me some money?’ ‘That depends. How much do you want?’ “你可不可以借点钱给我？”“那要看情况，你想要多少？” I don't know whether I'll see him. It depends what time he gets here. 我不知道会不会见到他。那要看他什么时间到达这里。 depend on sb/sth to be able to trust sb/sth to do sth; to rely on sb/sth 信赖；确信；依赖: If you ever need any help, you know you can depend on me. 如果你需要任何帮助，你知道我是信得过的。 You can't depend on the trains. They're always late. 那些火车经常误点，很不可靠。 I was depending on getting the money today. 我指望今天拿得到钱。 depend on sb/sth (for sth) to need sb/sth to provide sth 依靠；依赖: Our organization depends on donations from the public. 我们的机构依靠公众的捐助。 depend on sth to be decided or influenced by sb/sth 取决于；视…而定: His whole future depends on these exams. 他的前途完全取决于这些考试。

deposit¹
/dɪˈpɒzɪt ||; dɪˈpɑzɪt/verb[T]
1 to put sth down somewhere 放下；放置: He deposited his bags on the floor and sat down. 他把包放在地板上，然后坐下。
2 (used about liquid or a river) to leave sth lying on a surface, as the result of a natural or chemical process （指液体或河流）沉淀，淤积: mud deposited by a flood 洪水淤积的泥
3 to put money into an account at a bank 将（钱）存入银行: He deposited £20 a week into his savings account. 他每周把20英镑存入储蓄账户。
4 deposit sth (in sth);deposit sth (with sb/sth) to put sth valuable in an official place where it is safe until needed again （将贵重对象）存放，寄存（在安全地方）: Valuables can be deposited in the hotel safe. 贵重对象可寄存在酒店的保险箱内。
deposit²
/dɪˈpɒzɪt ||; dɪˈpɑzɪt/noun[C]
1 a deposit (on sth) a sum of money which is the first payment for sth, with the rest of the money to be paid later 订金: Once you have paid a deposit, the booking will be confirmed. 一经缴付订金便可确认预订。
2 a deposit (on sth) [usu.sing] a sum of money that you pay when you rent sth and get back when you return it without damage 保证金；押金: Boats can be hired for £5 an hour, plus £20 deposit. 船租每小时5英镑，另加押金20英镑。
3 a sum of money paid into a bank account 存款
4 a substance that has been left on a surface or in the ground as the result of a natural or chemical process 沉淀物；淤积物: mineral deposits 矿床

depot
/ˈdepəʊ; US ˈdi:pəʊ ||; ˈdipo/noun[C]
1 a place where large numbers of vehicles (buses, lorries, etc) are kept when not in use （公交车、卡车等的）车库
2 a place where large amounts of food, goods or equipment are stored 仓库；储藏处
3 (US 美) a small bus or railway station 公共汽车站；火车站

depraved
/dɪˈpreɪvd ||; dɪˈprevd/adj morally bad 道德败坏的；堕落的

depravity
/dɪˈprævəti ||; dɪˈprævətɪ/noun [U] (formal 正式) the state of being morally bad 道德败坏；腐化: a life of depravity 腐化生活

depreciate
/dɪˈpri:ʃieɪt ||; dɪˈpriʃɪˌet/verb [I] to become less valuable over a period of time （经过一段时间而）降价，贬值: New cars start to depreciate the moment they are on the road. 新汽车一上路就开始掉价。 ➔depreciation /dɪˌpri:ʃiˈeɪʃn ||; dɪˌpriʃɪˈeʃən/ noun [C,U]

depress
/dɪˈpres ||; dɪˈprɛs/verb[T]
1 to make sb unhappy and without hope or enthusiasm 使不快乐；使灰心；使失去热情: The thought of going to work tomorrow really depresses me. 我一想起明天要上班就十分沮丧。
2 (used about business) to cause sth to become less successful （指商业）使不景气，使萧条: The reduction in the number of tourists has depressed local trade. 游客人数下降已使本地生意变得萧条。
3 (formal 正式) to press sth down on a machine, etc 按下；压下: To switch off the machine, depress the lever. 要关机器，按下这杠杆。 ➔depressing adj The thought of growing old alone is very depressing. 想到孤孤单单地老起来令人十分沮丧。 ➔depressingly adv

depressed
/dɪˈprest ||; dɪˈprɛst/adj
1 very unhappy, often for a long period of time 沮丧的，忧愁的（往往指长时间）: He's been very depressed since he lost his job. 他失业以后变得很消沉。
2 (used about a place or an industry) without enough businesses or jobs （指地方或行业）不景气的，萧条的

depression
/dɪˈpreʃn ||; dɪˈprɛʃən/noun
1 [U] a feeling of unhappiness that lasts for a long time. Depression can be a medical condition and may have physical signs, for example being unable to sleep, etc 沮丧；消沉；抑郁症（有失眠等症状）: clinical/post-natal depression 临床╱产后抑郁症
2 [C,U] a period when the economic situation is bad, with little business activity and many people without a job 不景气；萧条（期）: The country was in the grip of (an) economic depression. 这个国家正处于经济萧条期。
3 [C] a part of a surface that is lower than the parts around it 凹地；坑: Rainwater collects in shallow depressions in the ground. 雨水积聚在地上的浅坑里。
4 [C] (technical术语) a weather condition in which the pressure of the air becomes lower, often causing rain 低气压 ☞Compare anticyclone. 与anticyclone比较。

deprive
/dɪˈpraɪv ||; dɪˈpraɪv/verb [T] deprive sb/sth of sth to prevent sb/sth from having sth; to take away sth from sb 使不能享有；剥夺；夺去: The prisoners were deprived of food. 那些囚犯被剥夺粮食。 ➔deprivation /ˌdeprɪˈveɪʃn ||; ˌdɛprɪˈveʃən/ noun [U]

deprived
/dɪˈpraɪvd ||; dɪˈpraɪvd/adj not having enough of the basic things in life, such as food, money, etc 贫困的: He came from a deprived background. 他自幼家境贫困。

Dept
abbr department 部门；（学校的）系: the Sales Dept 销售部

*depth
/depθ ||; dɛpθ/noun
1 [C,U] the distance down from the top to the bottom of sth 深，深度（指由顶至底的距离）: The hole should be 3cm in depth. 那个孔应是3厘米深。
2 [C,U] the distance from the front to the back of sth 纵深（指由前至后的距离）: the depth of a shelf 搁架的深度 ☞picture at length 见length插图
3 [U] the amount of emotion, knowledge, etc that a person has （感情、知识等的）深度: He tried to convince her of the depth of his feelings for her. 他努力使她相信他对她情深一片。
4 [C] [usu.pl] the deepest, most extreme or serious part of sth 最深的部份；最极端的部份；最严重的部份: in the depths of winter (= when it is coldest) 在隆冬 ☞adjective deep 形容词为deep
in depth looking at all the details; in a thorough way 深入；彻底: to discuss a problem in depth 深入地讨论问题 out of your depth
1 (Brit 英) in water that is too deep for you to stand up in 在水太深而不能站立的地方
2 in a situation that is too difficult for you 处于力所不及的情况: When they start discussing politics I soon get out of my depth. 他们开始讨论政治，我很快便茫然不知所云。

deputation
/ˌdepjəˈteɪʃn ||; ˌdɛpjəˈteʃən/noun [C] [with.sop] a group of people sent to sb to act or speak for others 代表团

deputize
/ˈdepjətaɪz ||; ˈdɛpjəˌtaɪz/ (also -ise) verb [I] deputize (for sb) to act for sb in a higher position, who is away or unable to do sth 代表；充当代理人

*deputy
/ˈdepjəti ||; ˈdɛpjətɪ/noun [C] (plural deputies) the second most important person in a particular organization, who does the work of his/her manager if the manager is away 代表；代理人；副手: the deputy head of a school 副校长

derail
/dɪˈreɪl ||; dɪˈrel/verb [T] to cause a train to come off a railway track 使（火车）出轨

derailment
/dɪˈreɪlmənt ||; dɪˈrelmənt/noun [C,U] an occasion when sth causes a train to come off a railway track （火车）出轨

deranged
/dɪˈreɪndʒd ||; dɪˈrendʒd/adj thinking and behaving in a way that is not normal, especially because of mental illness 精神错乱的，行为失常的（尤指由精神病引起）

derby
/ˈdɑ:bi ||; ˈdɑrbɪ/noun [C] (plural derbies)
1 (Brit 英) a race or sports competition 比赛；体育比赛: a motorcycle derby 摩托车比赛
2 (Brit 英) the Derby a horse race which takes place every year at Epsom 德比马赛（每年在英国埃普瑟姆举行）
3 (US 美) =BOWLER(1)

deregulate
/ˌdi:ˈregjuleɪt ||; diˈrɛgjəˌlet/verb [T] (often passive 常用于被动语态) to free a commercial or business activity from rules and controls 解除（对商业活动等的）控制，管制: deregulated financial markets 宽松的金融市场 ➔deregulation /ˌdi:ˌregjuˈleɪʃn ||; diˌrɛgjυˈleʃən/ noun [U]

derelict
/ˈderəlɪkt ||; ˈdɛrəˌlɪkt/adj no longer used and in bad condition 被废弃的；破旧不能用的: a derelict house 破败的房子

deride
/dɪˈraɪd ||; dɪˈraɪd/verb [T] to say that sb/sth is ridiculous; to laugh at sth in a cruel way 嘲弄；嘲笑；揶揄 ➔derision /dɪˈrɪʒn ||; dɪˈrɪʒən/ noun [U]: Her comments were met with derision. 她的意见受到嘲笑。 ➔derisive /dɪˈraɪsɪv ||; dɪˈraɪsɪv/ adj ‘What rubbish!’ he said with a derisive laugh. “真是废话！”他嘲笑着说。

derisory
/dɪˈraɪsəri ||; dɪˈraɪsərɪ/adj too small or of too little value to be considered seriously 小得可笑的；微不足道的: Union leaders rejected the derisory pay offer. 工会领袖拒绝了低得可笑的工资建议。

derivation
/ˌderɪˈveɪʃn ||; ˌdɛrəˈveʃən/noun [C,U] the origin from which a word or phrase has developed （词或短语的）派生，衍生

derivative
/dɪˈrɪvətɪv ||; dəˈrɪvətɪv/noun [C] a form of sth (especially a word) that has developed from the original form 派生物，衍生物（尤指派生词）: ‘Sadness’ is a derivative of ‘sad.’ sadness是sad的派生词。

derive
/dɪˈraɪv ||; dəˈraɪv/verb
1 [T] (formal 正式)derive sth from sth to get sth (especially a feeling or an advantage) from sth （从某物）取得，得到（尤指感觉或益处）: I derive great satisfaction from my work. 我从工作中得到很大的满足感。
2 [I,T] (used about a name or word) to come from sth; to have sth as its origin （指名字或词）从…而来，源出于 · The town derives its name from the river on which it was built. 这个市镇沿河而建，镇名来自那条河的名字。

dermatitis
/ˌdɜ:məˈtaɪtɪs ||; ˌdɝməˈtaɪtɪs/noun [U] a skin condition in which the skin becomes red, swollen and sore 皮炎

dermatologist
/ˌdɜ:məˈtɒlədʒɪst ||; ˌdɝməˈtɑlədʒɪst/noun [C] a doctor who studies and treats skin diseases 皮肤病医生

dermatology
/ˌdɜ:məˈtɒlədʒi ||; ˌdɝməˈtɑlədʒɪ/noun [U] the scientific study of skin diseases 皮肤病学 ➔dermatological /ˌdɜ:mətəˈlɒdʒɪkl ||; ˌdɝmətəˈlɑdʒɪkḷ/ adj

derogatory
/dɪˈrɒgətri; US -tɔ:rɪ ||; dɪˈrɑgəˌtɔrɪ/adj expressing a lack of respect for, or a low opinion of sth 不敬的；贬低的: derogatory comments about the standard of my work 贬低我工作水平的评语

desalination
/ˌdi:ˌsælɪˈneɪʃn ||; ˌdisæləˈneʃən/noun [U] the process of removing salt from sea water （海水的）脱盐，淡化

descant
/ˈdeskænt ||; ˈdɛskænt/noun [C] (in music) a tune that is sung or played at the same time as, and usually higher than, the main tune （音乐）多声部音乐中的上方声部（通常是高音部）

descend
/dɪˈsend ||; dɪˈsɛnd/verb [I,T] (formal 正式) to go down to a lower place; to go down sth 下来；下去；下降: The plane started to descend and a few minutes later we landed. 飞机开始下降，几分钟后我们便着陆了。 She descended the stairs slowly. 她慢慢地走下楼梯。 [OPP] opposite ascend 反义词为ascend be descended from sb to have sb as a relative in past times 是某人的后裔: He says he's descended from a Russian prince. 他说他是一位俄国王子的后代。

descendant
/dɪˈsendənt ||; dɪˈsɛndənt/noun [C] a person who belongs to the same family as sb who lived a long time ago 后裔；后代；子孙: Her family are descendants of one of the first Englishmen to arrive in America. 她的家族是首批来到美洲的英国人之一的后裔。 ☞Look at ancestor. 参看ancestor。

descent
/dɪˈsent ||; dɪˈsɛnt/noun
1 [C] a movement down to a lower place 下来；下去；下降: The pilot informed us that we were about to begin our descent. 机长通知我们说快要开始降落。
2 [U] a person's family origins 祖先；祖籍: He is of Italian descent. 他祖籍意大利。

*describe
/dɪˈskraɪb ||; dɪˈskraɪb/verb [T] describe sb/sth (to/for sb);describe sb/sth (as sth) to say what sb/sth is like, or what happened 描述；形容；叙述: Can you describe the bag you lost? 你可不可以描述一下你所遗失的手袋？ It's impossible to describe how I felt. 我没法形容我的感受。 The thief was described as tall, thin, and aged about twenty. 有人说那个贼身材高瘦，年约二十岁。

*description
/dɪˈskrɪpʃn ||; dɪˈskrɪpʃən/noun
1 [C,U] a picture in words of sb/sth or of sth that happened 描写；描述；叙述: The man gave the police a detailed description of the burglar. 那人向警方详尽地描述了那窃贼的模样。
2 [C] a type or kind of sth 种类；类型: It must be a tool of some description, but I don't know what it's for. 它定是某类工具，但我不知道它的用途。

descriptive
/dɪˈskrɪptɪv ||; dɪˈskrɪptɪv/adj that describes sb/sth, especially in a skilful or interesting way 描写的，叙述的（尤指巧妙地或生动地）: a piece of descriptive writing 一篇描写文 She gave a highly descriptive account of the journey. 她十分生动地叙述了那次旅程。

desecrate
/ˈdesɪkreɪt ||; ˈdɛsɪˌkret/verb [T] to damage a place of religious importance or treat it without respect 破坏，亵渎（圣地）: desecrated graves 被毁坏的坟墓 ➔desecration /ˌdesɪˈkreɪʃn ||; ˌdɛsɪˈkreʃən/ noun [U]: the desecration of a cemetery 毁坏公墓

*desert¹
/ˈdezət ||; ˈdɛzɚt/noun [C,U] a large area of land, usually covered with sand, that is hot and has very little water and very few plants 沙漠 ☞picture at ecosystem 见ecosystem插图
desert²
/dɪˈzɜ:t ||; dɪˈzɝt/verb
1 [T] to leave sb/sth, usually for ever 离开，抛弃（通常为永远地）: Many people have deserted the countryside and moved to the towns. 很多人已离开乡村搬进了市镇。
2 [I,T] (used especially about sb in the armed forces) to leave without permission （尤指军人）擅离职守，未经批准离开: He deserted because he didn't want to fight. 他因为不想打仗而擅自离开。 ➔desertion noun [C,U]

deserted
/dɪˈzɜ:tɪd ||; dɪˈzɝtɪd/adj empty, because all the people have left 无人居住的；荒废的: a deserted house 废弃的房子

deserter
/dɪˈzɜ:tə(r) ||; dɪˈzɝtɚ/noun [C] a person who leaves the armed forces without permission 逃兵

desertification
/dɪˌzɜ:tɪfɪˈkeɪʃn ||; dɪˌzɝtəfəˈkeʃən/noun [U] (technical术语) the process of becoming a desert or of making an area of land into a desert 沙漠化

ˌdesert ˈisland
noun [C] an island, especially a tropical one, where nobody lives 荒岛（尤指热带的）

*deserve
/dɪˈzɜ:v ||; dɪˈzɝv/verb [T] (not used in the continuous tenses 不用于进行时) to earn sth, either good or bad, because of sth that you have done 应受，应得（奖赏或惩罚）: We've done a lot of work and we deserve a break. 我们已经做了很多工作，应该休息一会儿。 He deserves to be punished severely for such a crime. 他犯了那种罪行，应该受到严厉的惩罚。 Although this verb is not used in the continuous tenses, it is common to see the present participle (= -ing form) There are other aspects of the case deserving attention. 虽然这个动词不用于进行时，但它的现在分词还是常见﹕There are other aspects of the case deserving attention. 这个案件的其他方面也值得注意。

deservedly
/dɪˈzɜ:vɪdli ||; dɪˈzɝvɪdlɪ/adv in a way that is right because of what sb has done 应得；理所当然: He deservedly won the Best Actor award. 他赢得最佳男演员的奖项是实至名归的。

deserving
/dɪˈzɜ:vɪŋ ||; dɪˈzɝvɪŋ/adj deserving (of sth) that you should give help, money, etc to 值得给予（帮助、钱等）的: This charity is a most deserving cause. 这是最值得赞助的慈善事业。

desiccated
/ˈdesɪkeɪtɪd ||; ˈdɛsəˌketd/adj
1 (used about food 指食物) dried in order to keep it for a long time 脱水的: desiccated coconut 脱水椰子
2 (technical术语) completely dry 干燥的；枯竭的: desiccated soil 干燥的土壤

desiccation
/ˌdesɪˈkeɪʃn ||; ˌdɛsəˈkeʃən/noun [U] the process of becoming completely dry 变干燥；变枯竭

*design¹
/dɪˈzaɪn ||; dɪˈzaɪn/noun
1 [U] the way in which sth is planned and made or arranged 设计；布局: Design faults have been discovered in the car. 那汽车被发现设计上有缺陷。
2 [U] the process and skill of making drawings that show how sth should be made, how it will work, etc 设计（术）；绘图（术）: to study industrial design 修读工业设计 graphic design 平面设计
3 [C] a design (for sth) a drawing or plan that shows how sth should be made, built, etc 图样；设计图: The architect showed us her design for the new theatre. 那位建筑师给我们看她设计的新剧院的图样。
4 [C] a pattern of lines, shapes, etc that decorate sth （作为装饰的）图案: a T-shirt with a geometric design on it 印有几何图案的T恤衫 [SYN] pattern 同义词为pattern
*design²
/dɪˈzaɪn ||; dɪˈzaɪn/verb
1 [I,T] to plan and make a drawing of how sth will be made 设计，绘制（图样） [T] to design cars/dresses/houses 设计汽车╱服装╱房屋
2 [T] to invent, plan and develop sth for a particular purpose 构思；计划: The bridge wasn't designed for such heavy traffic. 这座桥在设计上并没有准备要承受这么大的交通流量。

designate
/ˈdezɪgneɪt ||; ˈdɛzɪgˌnet/verb [T] (often passive 常用于被动语态) (formal 正式)
1 designate sth (as) sth to give sth a name to show that it has a particular purpose 命名；称为；定为: This has been designated (as) a conservation area. 这里已被列为保护区。
2 designate sb (as) sth to choose sb to do a particular job or task 指派；委任: Who has she designated (as) her deputy? 她委派谁当她的代表？
3 to show or mark sth 指明；标明；表示: These arrows designate the emergency exits. 这些箭头指示紧急出口。

ˌdesignated ˈdriver
noun [C] a person in a group who agrees not to drink alcohol and to drive the other members of the group home from a bar/party 指定驾车人﹙聚会等时不得饮酒以便可开车送他人回家的人﹚

ˌdesignated ˈhitter
noun [C] (in baseball 棒球) a person chosen to hit the ball instead of another player (the pitcher) 指定击球员

designer
/dɪˈzaɪnə(r) ||; dɪˈzaɪnɚ/noun [C] a person whose job is to make drawings or plans showing how sth will be made 设计师: a fashion/jewellery designer 时装╱珠宝设计师 designer jeans (= made by a famous designer) 由著名设计师设计的牛仔裤

desirable
/dɪˈzaɪərəbl ||; dɪˈzaɪrəbḷ/adj
1 wanted, often by many people; worth having 人们想要的；值得有的: Experience is desirable but not essential for this job. 做这份工作以有经验为佳，但并非必要。
2 sexually attractive 性感的 [OPP] undesirable 反义词为undesirable

desire¹
/dɪˈzaɪə(r) ||; dɪˈzaɪr/noun [C,U] (a) desire (for sth/to do sth)
1 the feeling of wanting sth very much; a strong wish 欲望；愿望；渴望 the desire for a peaceful solution to the crisis 对和平解决这危机的愿望 · I have no desire to visit that place again. 我不想再去那地方。
2 the wish for a sexual relationship with sb 性欲；情欲；肉欲
desire²
/dɪˈzaɪə(r) ||; dɪˈzaɪr/verb[T]
1 (formal 正式) (not used in the continuous tenses 不用于进行时) to want; to wish for 想要: They have everything they could possibly desire. 他们想要的已经都拥有。 The service in the restaurant left a lot to be desired (= was very bad). 那家餐馆的服务还有很多改进的余地。
2 to find sb/sth sexually attractive 觉得（某人或某物）性感动人
Although this verb is not used in the continuous tenses, it is common to see the present participle (= -ing form) Not desiring another argument, she turned away. 虽然这个动词不用于进行时，但它的现在分词还是常见﹕Not desiring another argument, she turned away. 她不想再次争吵，便转过脸去。
*desk
/desk ||; dɛsk/noun[C]
1 a type of table, often with drawers, that you sit at to write or work 书桌；写字台；办公桌: The pupils took their books out of their desks. 学生从书桌内拿出书本。 He used to be a pilot but now he has a desk job (= he works in an office). 他过去一直当飞行员，但现在坐写字台了。
2 a table or place in a building where a particular service is provided 工作台；服务台: an information desk 问讯处 Take your suitcases and tickets to the check-in desk. 拿着你的小提箱和机票到办理登机手续的服务台去。

ˈdesk clerk
noun [C] (US 美) = clerk(1)

desktop
/ˈdesktɒp ||; ˈdɛskˌtɑp/noun[C]
1 the top of a desk （办公桌的）桌面
2 a computer screen on which you can see symbols (icons) showing the programs, information, etc that are available to be used （计算机的）桌面
3 (also ˌdesktop comˈputer) a computer that can fit on a desk 台式计算机；桌面计算机 ☞Compare laptop and palm-top. 与laptop及palm-top比较。

ˌdesktop ˈpublishing
(abbr DTP) noun [U] the use of a small computer and a machine for printing, to produce books, magazines and other printed material 桌面出版（使用小型计算机和打印机出版书刊等）

desolate
/ˈdesələt ||; ˈdɛsḷɪt/adj
1 (used about a place) empty in a way that seems very sad （指地方）荒芜的，荒凉的: desolate wasteland 不毛之地
2 (used about a person) lonely, very unhappy and without hope （指人）孤苦绝望的 ➔desolation /ˌdesəˈleɪʃn ||; ˌdɛsəˈleʃən/ noun [U]: a scene of desolation 荒凉的景象 He felt utter desolation when his wife died. 他妻子死后他感到极其寂寞凄凉。

despair¹
/dɪˈspeə(r) ||; dɪˈspɛr/noun [U] the state of having lost all hope 完全失去希望；绝望: I felt like giving up in despair. 我感到绝望，很想放弃。 ➔despairing adj a despairing cry 绝望的呼叫 ☞Look at desperate. 参看desperate。
despair²
/dɪˈspeə(r) ||; dɪˈspɛr/verb [I] despair (of sb/sth) to lose all hope that sth will happen 完全失望；绝望: We began to despair of ever finding somewhere to live. 我们开始感到绝望，恐怕永远找不到住处了。

/dɪˈspætʃ ||; dɪˈspætʃ/ =DISPATCH

*desperate
/ˈdespərət ||; ˈdɛspərɪt/adj
1 out of control and ready to do anything to change the situation you are in because it is so terrible 铤而走险；（穷途末路而）不顾一切: She became desperate when her money ran out. 她的钱花光后，就不顾一切了。
2 done with little hope of success, as a last thing to try when everything else has failed 成功希望渺茫的；孤注一掷的: I made a desperate attempt to persuade her to change her mind. 我孤注一掷，企图劝她改变主意。
3 desperate (for sth/to do sth) wanting or needing sth very much 极想；极需要: Let's go into a cafe. I'm desperate for a drink. 一起去咖啡馆吧。我渴死了。
4 terrible, very serious 极坏的；十分严重的: There is a desperate shortage of skilled workers. 熟练工人极度缺乏。 ➔desperately adv She was desperately unlucky not to win. 她倒霉透顶，没有取胜。 ➔desperation /ˌdespəˈreɪʃn ||; ˌdɛspəˈreʃən/ noun [U]

despicable
/dɪˈspɪkəbl ||; dɪˈspɪkəbḷ/adj very unpleasant or evil 可憎的；可鄙的: a despicable act of terrorism 可鄙的恐怖主义行为

despise
/dɪˈspaɪz ||; dɪˈspaɪz/verb [T] to hate sb/sth very much 憎恨；厌恶；鄙视: I despise him for lying to me. 我恨他对我撒谎。

despite
/dɪˈspaɪt ||; dɪˈspaɪt/prep without being affected by the thing mentioned 尽管: Despite having very little money, they enjoy life. 尽管只有很少钱，他们仍然很享受生活。 The scheme went ahead despite public opposition. 虽然公众反对，这计划仍然实行了。 [SYN] in spite of 同义词为in spite of

/dɪˈspɒndənt ||; dɪˈspɑndənt/adj despondent (about/over sth) without hope; expecting no improvement 失望的；沮丧的；泄气的: She was becoming increasingly despondent about finding a job. 她对找工作越来越泄气。 ➔despondency /dɪˈspɒndənsi ||; dɪˈspɑndənsɪ/ noun [U]

/(also -ise) ˌdi:ˈsteɪbəlaɪz ||; dɪˈstebəˌlaɪz/verb [T] to make a system, government, country, etc become less safe and successful 使（制度、政府、国家等）不稳定；破坏…的稳定: Terrorist attacks were threatening to destabilize the government. 恐怖主义袭击有破坏政府安定之虞。 ☞Look at stabilize. 参看stabilize。

destined
/ˈdestɪnd ||; ˈdɛstɪnd/adj
1 destined for sth/to do sth having a future that has been decided or planned at an earlier time 命中注定: I think she is destined for success. 我想她是注定成功的。 He was destined to become one of the country's leading politicians. 他注定成为该国政坛要人之一。
2 destined for... travelling towards a particular place 往（某地）的；朝（某地）前进的: I boarded a bus destined for New York. 我上了一辆驶往纽约的公共汽车。

destiny
/ˈdestəni ||; ˈdɛstənɪ/noun (plural destinies)
1 [C] the things that happen to you in your life, especially things that you cannot control 天命；定数: She felt that it was her destiny to be a great singer. 她觉得自己命中注定要成为出色的歌手。
2 [U] a power that people believe controls their lives 命运 [SYN] fate 同义词为fate

*destroy
/dɪˈstrɔɪ ||; dɪˈstrɔɪ/verb[T]
1 to damage sth so badly that it can no longer be used or no longer exists 摧毁；毁坏；破坏: The building was destroyed by fire. 这座建筑物被大火焚毁了。 The defeat destroyed his confidence. 这次失败毁掉了他的信心。
2 to kill an animal, especially because it is injured or dangerous 杀死（尤指受伤或危险的动物）: The horse broke its leg and had to be destroyed. 那匹马弄断了腿，必须杀死。

*detail¹
/ˈdi:teɪl; US dɪˈteɪl ||; dɪˈtel/noun [C,U] one fact or piece of information 细节；详情: Just give me the basic facts. Don't worry about the details. 只告诉我基本事实就行，细节无须多说。 On the application form you should give details of your education and experience. 在申请表上必须详细填上你的学历和经验。 The work involves close attention to detail. 这工作须要密切注意每一个细节。 ➔detailed adj a detailed description 详细的描述 go into detail(s) to talk or write about the details of sth; to explain sth fully 详细说明；详述: I can't go into detail now because it would take too long. 我现在不能详细说明，因为这要花很多时间。 in detail including the details; thoroughly 详细地: We haven't discussed the matter in detail yet. 我们还没有详细地讨论这事。

/dɪˈteɪn ||; dɪˈten/verb [T] to stop sb from leaving a place; to delay sb 拘留；扣押；耽搁: A man has been detained by the police for questioning (= kept at the police station). 警方已将一名男子扣留加以审问。 Don't let me detain you if you're busy. 如果你忙着，我就不耽搁你了。 ☞Look at detention. 参看detention。

*determination
/dɪˌtɜ:mɪˈneɪʃn ||; dɪˌtɝməˈneʃən/noun [U]:
1 determination (to do sth) the quality of having firmly decided to do sth, even if it is very difficult 决心；决意: her determination to win 她要取得胜利的决心 You need great determination to succeed in business. 你须要很大的决心才能在商界取得成功。
2 (formal 正式) the process of deciding sth officially （正式）决定: the determination of future government policy 未来政府政策的决定

determine
/dɪˈtɜ:mɪn ||; dɪˈtɝmɪn/verb[T]
1 (formal 正式) to discover the facts about sth 查明（事实真相）: We need to determine what happened immediately before the accident. 我们须要查明事故发生前不久的情形。
2 to make sth happen in a particular way or be of a particular type 决定；确定: The results of the tests will determine what treatment you need. 这些化验的结果会决定你需要哪种治疗方法。 Age and experience will be determining factors in our choice of candidate. 年龄和经验将是我们选择候选人的决定因素。
3 (formal 正式) to decide sth officially （正式）确定，决定: A date for the meeting has yet to be determined. 会议的日期还得确定一下。

*determined
/dɪˈtɜ:mɪnd ||; dɪˈtɝmɪnd/adj determined (to do sth) having firmly decided to do sth or to succeed, even if it is difficult 决意的；坚决的: He is determined to leave school, even though his parents want him to stay. 虽然他的父母要他继续读书，但他决心辍学。 She's a very determined athlete. 她是个意志十分坚决的运动员。

/dɪˈtɜ:mɪnə(r) ||; dɪˈtɝmɪnɚ/noun [C] (grammar语法) a word that comes before a noun to show how the noun is being used 限定符（置于名词前，用于显示该名词用法）: ‘Her’, ‘most’ and ‘those’ are all determiners. her、most及those都是限定符。

/ˈdevəsteɪtɪŋ ||; ˈdɛvəsˌtetɪŋ/adj

*develop
/dɪˈveləp ||; dɪˈvɛləp/verb
1 [I,T] to grow slowly, increase, or change into sth else; to make sb/sth do this （使）成长；（使）发育；发展 [I] to develop from a child into an adult 由儿童长大成人 [T] a scheme to help pupils develop their natural talents 帮助学生发展天赋的计划 Scientists have developed a drug against this disease. 科学家已经研制出一种治疗这种疾病的药物。 Over the years, she's developed her own unique singing style. 这些年来，她已经形成自己独特的唱歌风格。
2 [I,T] to begin to have a problem or disease; to start to affect sth 开始出现（问题）；患上（疾病）；开始影响（某物） [T] to develop cancer/Aids 患上癌症╱艾滋病 Trouble is developing along the border. 边境开始出现麻烦。
3 [T] to make an idea, a story, etc clearer or more detailed by writing or talking about it more 更详尽阐述；使展开；发挥: She went on to develop this theme later in the lecture. 她在讲课中接着更详尽地阐述了这个主题。
4 [T] to make pictures or negatives from a piece of film by using special chemicals 冲洗（照片）: to develop a film 冲洗胶卷
5 [T] to build houses, shops, factories, etc on a piece of land 开发（土地，在上面兴建房屋、商店、工厂等）: This site is being developed for offices. 这工地现正兴建办公楼。

/dɪˈveləpt ||; dɪˈvɛləpt/adj of a good level or standard 已发展的；发达的；已开发的: a highly developed economy 高度发达的经济

/dɪˈveləpə(r) ||; dɪˈvɛləpɚ/ (also property developer) noun [C] a person or company that builds houses, shops, etc on a piece of land 土地开发商；土地开发公司；房地产开发商

developing
/dɪˈveləpɪŋ ||; dɪˈvɛləpɪŋ/adj (used about a poor country) that is trying to develop or improve its economy （指穷国）发展中的，开发中的: a developing country 发展中国家 the developing world 发展中世界

*development
/dɪˈveləpmənt ||; dɪˈvɛləpmənt/noun
1 [U] the process of becoming bigger, stronger, better etc, or of making sb/sth do this 发育；发展；培育；开发: the development of tourism in Cuba 古巴旅游业的发展 a child's intellectual development 儿童的智力发展
2 [U] [C] the process of creating sth more advanced; a more advanced product 研制更先进的产品；更先进的产品: She works in research and development for a drug company. 她在一家医药公司从事研究和开发工作。 the latest developments in space technology 航天技术的最新成果
3 [C] a new event that changes a situation 新情况；事态发展: This week has seen a number of new developments in the Middle East. 这星期中东形势有几个新发展。
4 [C,U] a piece of land with new buildings on it; the process of building on a piece of land 新开发区；开发（土地）: a new housing development 新建住宅区: The land has been bought for development. 这块土地已经买下来进行开发。

deviant
/ˈdi:viənt ||; ˈdivɪənt/adj different from what most people consider to be normal and acceptable 偏常的；不正常的: deviant behaviour 偏常行为 ➔deviant noun [C]:sexual deviants 性变态者 ➔deviance /ˈdi:viəns ||; ˈdivɪəns/ ➔deviancy /ˈdi:viənsi ||; ˈdivɪənsɪ/ noun [U]: a study of social deviance and crime 对社会偏常和犯罪现象的研究

deviate
/ˈdi:vieɪt ||; ˈdivɪˌet/verb [I] deviate (from sth) to change or become different from what is normal or expected 背离；偏离: He never once deviated from his original plan. 他从没有偏离他原先的计划。

deviation
/ˌdi:viˈeɪʃn ||; ˌdivɪˈeʃən/noun [C,U] a difference from what is normal or expected, or from what is approved of by society 偏差；背离；逸出常轨: sexual deviation 性变态 [C]:a deviation from our usual way of doing things 偏离我们通常的做法

*device
/dɪˈvaɪs ||; dɪˈvaɪs/noun[C]
1 a tool or piece of equipment made for a particular purpose （为特定用途制造的）工具，装置，设备，仪器: a security device which detects any movement 可探测出任何活动的保安装置 labour-saving devices such as washing machines and vacuum cleaners 节省人力的设备，如洗衣机和吸尘器 ☞Look at the note at tool. 参看tool的注释。
2 a clever method for getting the result you want 巧妙办法；策略: Critics dismissed the speech as a political device for winning support. 批评者认为那篇演说不过是用以博取支持的政治把戏。

devil
/ˈdevl ||; ˈdɛvḷ/noun[C]
1 the Devil the most powerful evil being, according to the Christian, Jewish and Muslim religions 魔鬼；撒旦 ☞Look at Satan. 参看Satan。
2 an evil being; a spirit 魔鬼；恶魔
3 (spoken 口语) a word used to show pity, anger, etc when you are talking about a person （谈到某人时用以表示怜悯、愤怒等）家伙，人: The poor devil died in hospital two days later. 那可怜的家伙两天后在医院死去。 Those kids can be little devils sometimes. 那些孩子有时候会有点儿淘气。
be a devil used to encourage sb to do sth that he/she is not sure about doing （用于鼓励某人去干其拿不定主意的事）: Go on, be a devil -- buy both of them. 买吧，别犹豫──把这两样都买下来。 speak/talk of the devil used when the person who is being talked about appears unexpectedly （指说到某人，某人突然出现）说曹操，曹操就到

devious
/ˈdi:viəs ||; ˈdivɪəs/adj clever but not honest or direct 狡猾的；不诚实的；不正直的: I wouldn't trust him -- he can be very devious. 我不会信任他─他为人很狡猾。 a devious trick/plan 奸计；诡计 ➔deviously adv

devise
/dɪˈvaɪz ||; dɪˈvaɪz/verb [T] to invent a new way of doing sth 想出，发明（新办法）: They've devised a plan for keeping traffic out of the city centre. 他们已经想出一个计划来让车辆进不了市中心。

devoid
/dɪˈvɔɪd ||; dɪˈvɔɪd/adj (formal 正式)devoid of sth not having a particular quality; without sth 缺少…的；没有…的: devoid of hope/ambition/imagination 没有希望╱雄心╱想象力

devolution
/ˌdi:vəˈlu:ʃn; US ˌdev- ||; ˌdɛvəˈluʃən/noun [U] the act of giving political power from central to local government （中央政府向地方政府的）权力下放 ☞verb devolve 动词为devolve

devolve
/dɪˈvɒlv ||; dɪˈvɑlv/verb devolve on/upon sb/sth(written 书面语)
1 if property, money, etc devolves on/upon you, you receive it after sb dies （财产、钱财等）转让，被继承
2 if a duty, responsibility, etc devolves on/upon you, it is given to you by sb at a higher level of authority （职责、责任等）被上级交给
devolve sth to/on/upon sb to give a duty, responsibility, power, etc to sb who has less authority than you 把（职责、责任、权力等）交给下级: The central government devolved most tax-raising powers to the regional authorities. 中央政府把大部份征税权交给了地方当局。 ☞noun devolution 名词为devolution

devote
/dɪˈvəʊt ||; dɪˈvot/verb [T] devote yourself/sth to sb/sth to give a lot of time, energy, etc to sb/sth 奉献（许多时间、精力等）；致力于；献身于: She gave up work to devote herself full-time to her music. 她放弃了工作，专心搞音乐。 Schools should devote more time to science subjects. 学校应该多排点时间给理科科目。

devoted
/dɪˈvəʊtɪd ||; dɪˈvotɪd/adj devoted (to sb/sth) loving sb/sth very much; completely loyal to sb/sth 热爱的；深爱的；完全忠于…的: Neil's absolutely devoted to his wife. 尼尔全心全意地爱他的妻子。

/ˌdevəˈti: ||; ˌdɛvəˈti/noun [C] a devotee (of sb/sth) a person who likes sb/sth very much 仰慕者；爱好者；热心者: Devotees of science fiction will enjoy this new film. 科幻小说的爱好者会喜欢这部新片。

devotion
/dɪˈvəʊʃn ||; dɪˈvoʃən/noun [U]: devotion (to sb/sth)
1 great love for sb/sth 挚爱；热爱: a mother's devotion to her children 母亲对子女深深的疼爱
2 the act of giving a lot of your time, energy, etc to sb/sth 忠心；热心；献身: devotion to duty 忠于职守
3 very strong religious feeling 虔诚

dictate
/dɪkˈteɪt; US ˈdɪkteɪt ||; ˈdɪktet/verb
1 [I,T] dictate (sth) (to sb) to say sth aloud so that sb else can write or type it 口授；读出（文字，让别人听写） [T] to dictate a letter to a secretary 向秘书口授信稿
2 [I,T] dictate (sth) (to sb) to tell sb what to do in a way that seems unfair 专横地指示；专横地命令 · Parents can't dictate to their children how they should run their lives. 父母不能强行规定子女应该怎样生活。
3 [T] to control or influence sth 支配；影响: The kind of house people live in is usually dictated by how much they earn. 人住什么样的房子通常是由他们挣钱多少决定的。

*die
/daɪ ||; daɪ/verb (present participle dying third person singular present dies;past tense past participle died)
1 [I,T] die (from/of sth) to stop living 死去；死亡: My father died when I was three. 我父亲在我三岁时死去。 Thousands of people have died from this disease. 已经有数以千计的人死于这种疾病。 [I] to die of hunger 死于饥饿 [I] to die for what you believe in 为信仰而死 [T] to die a natural/violent death 自然死；暴力致死 ☞adjective dead, noun death. 形容词为dead，名词为death
2 [I] to stop existing; to disappear 不复存在；消失: The old customs are dying. 旧的习俗正在消亡。 Our love will never die. 我们的爱情天长地久。
be dying for sth/to do sth(spoken 口语) to want sth/to do sth very much 极想；渴望: I'm dying for a cup of coffee. 我真想喝杯咖啡。 die hard to change or disappear only slowly or with difficulty 难改变；难消灭: Old attitudes towards women die hard. 对女性的旧观念很难改过来。 to die for(informal 非正式) if you think that sth is to die for, you really want it and would do anything to get it 竭力想弄到手的；极好的: They have a house in town that's to die for. 他们在城里有一幢好得要命的房子。 die laughing to find sth very funny 觉得很有趣: I thought I'd die laughing when he told that joke. 他讲的那个笑话我觉得好笑得要命。 die away to slowly become weaker before stopping or disappearing 变弱；渐渐停止；逐渐消失: The sound of the engine died away as the car drove into the distance. 那辆汽车越走越远，引擎的声音也随之逐渐消失。 die down to slowly become less strong 变弱；渐渐平息；缓和: Let's wait until the storm dies down before we go out. 我们等到风暴平息以后再出去吧。 die off to die one by one until there are none left 相继死去 die out to stop happening or disappear 不再发生；消失: The use of horses on farms has almost died out in this country. 这个国家的农场几乎已不再用马帮助农务。

diesel
/ˈdi:zl ||; ˈdizḷ/noun
1 [U] a type of heavy oil used in some engines instead of petrol 柴油: a diesel engine 柴油机 a taxi that runs on diesel 用柴油的出租车
2 [C] a vehicle that uses diesel 用柴油的车辆: My new car's a diesel. 我的新车使用柴油。 ☞Look at petrol. 参看petrol。

*diet¹
/ˈdaɪət ||; ˈdaɪət/noun
1 [C,U] the food that a person or animal usually eats 日常食物；日常饮食: They live on a diet of rice and vegetables. 他们的日常食物是大米和蔬菜。 I always try to have a healthy, balanced diet (= including all the different types of food that our body needs). 我总是设法做到饮食均衡健康。 Poor diet is a cause of ill health. 饮食营养不足是健康欠佳的原因之一。
2 [C] certain foods that a person who is ill, or who wants to lose weight is allowed to eat （因患病或为减肥而设的）规定饮食，特种食谱: a low-fat diet 低脂肪食谱 a sugar-free diet 无糖食谱 ➔dietary /ˈdaɪətəri ||; ˈdaɪəˌtɛrɪ/ adj dietary habits/requirements 饮食习惯╱要求
be/go on a diet to eat only certain foods or a small amount of food because you want to lose weight 节食
diet²
/ˈdaɪət ||; ˈdaɪət/verb [I] to try to lose weight by eating less food or only certain kinds of food 节食: You've lost some weight. Have you been dieting? 你的体重减轻了。你是否在节食？

dietetics
/ˌdaɪəˈtetɪks ||; ˌdaɪəˈtɛtɪks/noun [U] the scientific study of the food we eat and its effect on our health 饮食学；膳食学

differ
/ˈdɪfə(r) ||; ˈdɪfɚ/verb[I]
1 differ (from sb/sth) to be different 不同于；异于: How does this car differ from the more expensive model? 这辆车与那种较昂贵的型号有什么不同？
2 differ (with sb) (about/on sth) to have a different opinion 不同意；持异议: I'm afraid I differ with you on that question. 在那个问题上我与你恐怕看法不同。

*difference
/ˈdɪfrəns ||; ˈdɪfrəns/noun
1 [C] a difference (between A and B) the way that people or things are not the same or the way that sb/sth has changed 差别；差异；不同之处: What's the difference between this computer and that cheaper one? 这台计算机与那台较便宜的有什么不同？ From a distance it's hard to tell the difference between the twins. 从远处看很难区分这对双胞胎。
2 [C,U] difference (in sth) (between A and B) the amount by which people or things are not the same or by which sb/sth has changed （数量上的）差，差额，差距: There's an age difference of three years between the two children. 这两名儿童相差三岁。 There's very little difference in price since last year. 去年以来价格的变化不大。 We gave a 30% deposit and must pay the difference when the work is finished (= the rest of the money). 我们付了30%作为订金，余额则须在完工时缴付。
3 [C] a disagreement that is not very serious 不同的意见；分歧；轻微的争执: All couples have their differencesfrom time to time. 所有夫妻都免不了偶尔有不同意见。 There was a difference of opinion over how much we owed. 我们究竟欠多少，对这个问题存在不同看法。
make a, some, etc difference (to sb/sth) to have an effect (on sb/sth) 对…有影响；对…起作用: Marriage made a big difference to her life. 婚姻在很大程度上改变了她的生活。 make no difference (to sb/sth);not make any difference to not be important (to sb/sth); to have no effect 对…并不重要；对…无影响: It makes no difference to us if the baby is a girl or a boy. 对我们来说生男生女都一样。 split the difference→SPLIT¹

*different
/ˈdɪfrənt ||; ˈdɪfrənt/adj
1 different (from/to sb/sth) not the same 不同的；相异的: The play was different from anything I had seen before. 这出戏和我以前所看过的都不同。 The two houses are very different in style. 这两幢房子在风格上很不同。 You'd look completely different with short hair. 你要是留短发会面目一新。 When Ulf started school in this country, the other kids were cruel to him because he was different. 乌尔夫刚在这个国家上学时，别的孩子都虐待他，因为他与众不同。 [OPP] similar 反义词为similar ☞In American English different than is also used. 美国英语亦作different than。
2 separate; individual 分别的；各不相同的；个别的: This coat is available in three different colours. 这款大衣有三种不同的颜色可供选择。 ➔differently adv I think you'll feel differently about it tomorrow. 我想明天你对它会有不同的感觉。

differential¹
/ˌdɪfəˈrenʃl ||; ˌdɪfəˈrɛnʃəl/noun[C]
1 a differential (between A and B) a difference in the amount, value or size of sth, especially the difference in rates of pay for people doing different work in the same industry or profession 差别（尤指同一行业中不同工种的工资差别）
2 (also ˌdifferential ˈgear) a GEAR that makes it possible for a vehicle's back wheels to turn around at different speeds when going around corners （汽车的）分速器，差速器
differential²
/ˌdɪfəˈrenʃl ||; ˌdɪfəˈrɛnʃəl/adj (only before a noun 只用于名词前) (formal 正式) showing or depending on a difference; not equal 差别的；依差别而定的；不平等的

differentiate
/ˌdɪfəˈrenʃieɪt ||; ˌdɪfəˈrɛnʃɪˌet/verb
1 [I,T] differentiate between A and B;differentiate A (from B) to see or show how things are different 区分；区别；辨别: It is hard to differentiate between these two types of seed. 这两类种子很难区别开来。
2 [T] differentiate sth (from sth) to make one thing different from another 使不同；使有差别: The coloured feathers differentiate the male bird from the plain brown female. 这种鸟的雌雄从羽毛的颜色区分得出来，雄性是彩色的，雌性是纯褐色的。 [SYN] distinguish 同义词为distinguish
3 [I] to treat one person or group differently from another 区别对待: We don't differentiate between the two groups -- we treat everybody alike. 我们对待两组没有差别，都一视同仁。 [SYN] discriminate 同义词为discriminate ➔differentiation /ˌdɪfəˌrenʃiˈeɪʃn ||; ˌdɪfəˌrɛnʃɪˈeʃən/ noun [U]

*difficult
/ˈdɪfɪkəlt ||; ˈdɪfəkəlt/adj
1 difficult (for sb) (to do sth) not easy to do or understand 困难的；难懂的: a difficult test/problem 困难的测验；难题 I find it difficult to get up early in the morning. 我觉得早上很难早起。 It was difficult for us to hear the speaker. 我们很难听清演讲者在说些什么。 I'm in a difficult situation. Whatever I do, somebody will be upset. 我的处境很困难。无论我干什么都会有人不高兴。
2 (used about a person) not friendly, reasonable or helpful （指人）不随和的，不友好的，难相处的: a difficult customer 难以讨好的顾客

*difficulty
/ˈdɪfɪkəlti ||; ˈdɪfəkəltɪ/noun (plural difficulties)
1 [U,C] difficulty (in sth/in doing sth) a problem; a situation that is hard to deal with 难题；难事；困难: I'm sure you won't have any difficultygetting a visa for America. 我敢肯定，你申请签证往美国不会遇到任何困难。 We had no difficulty selling our car. 我们毫不费事便把车子卖掉了。 We found a hotel without difficulty. 我们不费吹灰之力便找到了一家旅馆。 With difficulty, I managed to persuade Alice to lend us the money. 我好不容易才说服艾丽斯借钱给我们。· I could see someone in difficulty in the water so I went to help them. 我见到有人掉在水里上不来，所以我就去救援。 [pl] If you borrow too much money you may get into financial difficulties. 借钱太多很可能会令你陷入经济困境。
2 [U] how hard sth is to do or to deal with 难度: The questions start easy and then increase in difficulty. 开头的问题比较容易，后面的问题就越来越难。

*dig¹
/dɪg ||; dɪg/verb [I,T] (present participle digging;past tense past participle dug /dʌg ||; dʌg/) to move earth and make a hole in the ground 挖；掘: The children are busy digging in the sand. 这些小孩忙于在沙地上挖洞。 [T] to dig a hole 挖洞 dig deep to try harder, give more, go further, etc than is usually necessary 更努力；给更多；更深入: Charities for the homeless are asking people to dig deep into their pockets in this cold weather. 在这种寒冷的天气里，慈善机构要求人们为无家可归的人捐助更多的钱。 dig your heels in to refuse to do sth or to change your mind about sth 拒绝（干某事）；固执己见: The union dug its heels in and waited for a better pay offer. 工会的立场很坚定，工资不提高一点就不罢休。 dig (sth) in; dig sth into sth to push or press (sth) into sb/sth 把…插入或按入: My neck is all red where my collar is digging in. 我脖子上领子套着的地方红得厉害。 He dug his hands deep into his pockets. 他把两手深深插进口袋里。 dig sb/sth out (of sth)
1 to get sb/sth out of sth by moving the earth, etc that covers him/her/it 掘出；挖出: Rescue workers dug the survivors out of the rubble. 救援人员把幸存者从瓦砾中挖掘出来。
2 to get or find sb/sth by searching 探索；找出；发现: Bill went into the attic and dug out some old photos. 比尔进了阁楼，找出来一些旧照片。
dig sth up
1 to remove sth from the earth by digging 掘出；挖出；采掘: to dig up potatoes 掘出马铃薯
2 to make a hole or take away soil by digging 挖掘土地: Workmen are digging up the road in front of our house. 工人正在我们的房子前面掘路。
3 to find information by searching or studying 找到，查明（数据）: Newspapers have dug up some embarrassing facts about his private life. 报章揭露了一些有关他私生活的尴尬事情。
dig²
/dɪg ||; dɪg/noun
1 [C] a hard push 推；捅；戳；刺: to give sb a dig in the ribs (= with your elbow) 用力戳某人的肋部一下（用手肘）
2 [C] something that you say to upset sb 挖苦的话；讽刺的话: The others kept making digs at him because of the way he spoke. 他那种说话方式惹来其他人不断的挖苦。
3 [C] an occasion or place where a group of people try to find things of historical or scientific interest in the ground in order to study them 考古发掘的场合或地点: an archaeological dig 考古发掘现场
